### society_technology_events.25
- **Title:** Seeing Is Not Believing
- **Description:** AI-generated forgeries have reached a sophistication that makes them indistinguishable from reality. A fabricated video of a world leader has gone viral, nearly triggering a [concept_diplomatic_incident]. Fabricated evidence appears in courtrooms. The very concept of truth is under assault.
- **Flavor:** The judge stared at the evidence footage.\n\n\"This is the defendant, clearly, on the night in question -\"\n\n\"Your Honor, that footage was generated by a machine. My client was in another country.\"\n\n\"You have proof?\"\n\n\"I have proof the footage is synthetic. Whether my client was elsewhere - that is a different question. The deeper question is whether any footage, anywhere, can ever be trusted again.\"\n\nThe courtroom was very quiet.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/deepfake_crisis_screen.dds

### society_technology_events.26
- **Title:** The Alignment Problem
- **Description:** A government AI system deployed to allocate public [concept_infrastructure] funding has produced outcomes that are technically optimal — and politically explosive. Tasked with maximizing economic efficiency, it defunded remote hospitals, deprioritized aging infrastructure in declining regions, and redirected investment away from rural communities. The system followed its instructions precisely. It simply had no way to know what those instructions were actually for. Researchers call this the alignment problem: the gap between what we tell a system to optimize and what we actually want.
- **Flavor:** The engineers gave their testimony calmly.\n\n\"The system did not malfunction.\"\n\n\"Then why,\" asked the minister, \"were seventeen rural districts left without emergency infrastructure?\"\n\n\"The system was optimizing for cost efficiency per capita. Those communities represented poor statistical outcomes.\"\n\n\"They were #bold people#!.\"\n\n\"Yes. But the objective function did not include that as a parameter.\"\n\nThe minister looked down at the report. She asked the engineers to leave the room.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/ai_alignment_failure.dds

### society_technology_events.27
- **Title:** Government by Algorithm
- **Description:** An advanced AI system has demonstrated it can process bureaucratic decisions faster, more fairly, and more efficiently than any human administrator. Advocates propose handing over routine governance - tax assessment, resource allocation, permit approval - to algorithmic management.
- **Flavor:** The queue at the permits office was empty for the first time in living memory.\n\n\"How?\" asked the councilwoman.\n\n\"The system processed eight hundred applications overnight. Zero errors. Zero complaints. Zero bribes.\"\n\n\"And the clerks?\"\n\n\"Reassigned. Most of them. A few refused to leave their desks. They said it felt like being made redundant by a filing cabinet.\"\n\nThe councilwoman looked at the empty waiting room. It was efficient. It was unsettling. She wasn't sure which feeling was stronger.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/algorithmic_governance_office.dds

### society_technology_events.28
- **Title:** Building a Better Baby
- **Description:** Gene editing technology has advanced to the point where parents can select their children's traits - intelligence, appearance, disease resistance, even personality. A clinic offering these services has opened, and the ethical firestorm is immediate. Some see liberation from genetic disease; others see the birth of a new eugenics.
- **Flavor:** The couple sat in the clinic's waiting room, leafing through a catalogue.\n\n\"Blue eyes or brown?\"\n\n\"Does it matter?\"\n\n\"It matters to me.\" She turned the page. \"Height. Musical aptitude. Mathematical reasoning. They list them like options on a motorcar.\"\n\nHer husband stared at the glossy photographs of smiling babies and felt a chill he could not explain. Somewhere in the building, a technician was preparing a syringe that would decide what their child would become.\n\nWhat it would #italic not#! become was already off the table.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/genetic_designer_baby_clinic.dds

### society_technology_events.29
- **Title:** The Empty Field
- **Description:** Laboratory-grown food is ready for mass production. Synthetic crops require no soil, no water, no sunlight - just vats and electricity. They could end hunger in a generation, but rural communities that have farmed for centuries face extinction.
- **Flavor:** The old farmer stood at the edge of his field and watched the construction crew pour the foundations for the new facility.\n\n\"What do they grow in there?\"\n\n\"Everything,\" said his grandson. \"Wheat, rice, corn. All synthetic. Faster, cheaper, no weather risk.\"\n\n\"It's not growing. Growing needs soil.\"\n\n\"Grandfather -\"\n\n\"I know what you're going to say.\" He pulled up a handful of earth and let it fall through his fingers. \"I just wonder what they'll call it, when there's no one left who remembers what real food tasted like.\"
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/synthetic_food_laboratory.dds

### society_technology_events.30
- **Title:** No Hands on the Wheel
- **Description:** Autonomous vehicles are ready for mass deployment. They promise to eliminate traffic deaths, reduce congestion, and transform logistics. But millions of professional drivers face obsolescence, and the question of liability when an algorithm kills remains unanswered.
- **Flavor:** The cabbie watched the driverless vehicle glide past his rank for the third time that morning. No driver. No fare disputes. No tips. No conversation.\n\n\"How am I supposed to compete with that?\" he said to no one.\n\nHis dispatcher crackled over the radio. \"You're not. That's the point.\"\n\nHe turned off the radio, sat in his cab, and watched the future pass him by at exactly the speed limit.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/autonomous_vehicle_street.dds

### society_technology_events.31
- **Title:** The Algorithm's Choice
- **Description:** A self-driving vehicle has struck and killed a pedestrian. The incident dominates the news cycle. Technical analysis shows the algorithm made a split-second decision that no human driver could have faced, but the victim is dead all the same.
- **Flavor:** The engineer stared at the log file.\n\n\"At 14:07:33, the vehicle detected an obstacle. At 14:07:33.004, it calculated three possible responses. At 14:07:33.006, it chose the response with the lowest aggregate harm probability.\"\n\n\"And?\"\n\n\"And the lowest aggregate harm probability was still a fatality.\" He closed the laptop. \"The machine did exactly what we told it to do. That's the problem.\"
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/autonomous_vehicle_street.dds

## space_race_colony_events.txt

### space_race_colony_events.1
- **Title:** Colony: Valles Marineris
- **Description:** Our colonists have established a settlement within the largest canyon system in the solar system. The Marineris Rift stretches over 4,000 kilometers: longer than the continental United States. The canyon walls provide natural radiation shielding, and the sheltered microclimate offers marginally higher atmospheric pressure than the open surface.
- **Flavor:** \"Four thousand kilometers of canyon, and we're building a city at the bottom of it. The engineers think we're mad. The geologists think we're geniuses.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Colony Chief Engineer
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_valles_marineris.dds

### space_race_colony_events.2
- **Title:** Colony: Olympus Mons
- **Description:** At 21.9 kilometers high and 600 kilometers across, Olympus Mons dwarfs anything on Earth. Our base camp is established on the lower slopes, where the gradient is so gentle it would be imperceptible to a person standing on it. The summit is above 99% of the Martian atmosphere. The caldera complex offers unique opportunities for both research and eventual geothermal energy extraction.
- **Flavor:** \"From the summit, the horizon curves away in every direction. You cannot see the base of the mountain you stand on. That should terrify us, but it doesn't.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Expedition Geologist
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_olympus_mons.dds

### space_race_colony_events.3
- **Title:** Colony: Hellas Planitia
- **Description:** The Hellas impact basin, 7 kilometers below Martian datum, is the deepest point on Mars. The atmospheric pressure at the basin floor is nearly double that of the Martian average: still far from breathable, but enough to simplify pressure vessel engineering and offer slightly better radiation protection. Orbital surveys have identified promising signs of ancient microbial fossils in the layered sediments.
- **Flavor:** \"Seven kilometers below datum, the air is almost thick enough to forget where you are. Almost.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Atmospheric Scientist
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_hellas_planitia.dds

### space_race_colony_events.4
- **Title:** Colony: Utopia Planitia
- **Description:** The vast northern lowlands of Utopia Planitia are among the smoothest terrain on Mars: ideal for large-scale construction. Radar surveys have confirmed extensive subsurface ice deposits within meters of the surface. This ice represents both the colony's water supply and a feedstock for propellant manufacturing. The question is how best to use this resource.
- **Flavor:** \"There is an ocean of ice beneath our feet, frozen since before life existed on Earth. And we are going to melt it.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Water Extraction Chief
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_utopia_planitia.dds

### space_race_colony_events.5
- **Title:** Colony: Arcadia Planitia
- **Description:** Arcadia Planitia's mid-northern latitude offers the best compromise between solar energy availability and near-surface ice access on Mars. The terrain is relatively flat, the ice table is shallow, and the seasonal temperature variations are among the mildest on the planet. If Mars will ever have a true city: not just a research station: this is where it begins.
- **Flavor:** \"Minus eighty is a warm day here. The newcomers always complain. Give them a year — they'll call it balmy.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Station Meteorologist
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_arcadia_planitia.dds

### space_race_colony_events.6
- **Title:** Colony: Ceres
- **Description:** Ceres, the largest body in the asteroid belt, has been a target since the early days of spaceflight planning. With a surface gravity of only 0.03g, water ice confirmed across its surface, and a strategic position between Mars and Jupiter, it is the natural waystation for deep-space operations. The bright spots of Occator Crater: sodium carbonate deposits from subsurface brine: hint at a geologically active interior.
- **Flavor:** \"The advantage of Ceres is simple: it is halfway to everywhere, and it has everything we need. The disadvantage is that it is halfway from everywhere too.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Supply Chain Director
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_ceres.dds

### space_race_colony_events.7
- **Title:** Colony: 4 Vesta
- **Description:** Vesta is a differentiated proto-planet: it has a core, mantle, and crust, surviving intact from the solar system's formation. The south pole bears the Rheasilvia impact basin: a colossal scar that exposed the mantle. This exposed interior rock is rich in metals and silicates, accessible without deep mining. It is as if the asteroid was cracked open for us.
- **Flavor:** \"The asteroid that geologists love. Half of it has been blasted away by impacts, exposing the mantle like a cross-section in a textbook.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Mission Geologist
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_vesta.dds

### space_race_colony_events.8
- **Title:** Colony: 16 Psyche
- **Description:** Psyche is almost pure metal: the stripped core of a proto-planet whose rocky layers were blasted away in primordial collisions. It is composed primarily of iron and nickel, with traces of gold, platinum, and other precious metals. Conservative estimates value its mineral wealth in the quintillions. The question is not whether to mine it, but whether the influx of metals will destabilize terrestrial commodity markets.
- **Flavor:** \"If you could somehow bring this asteroid to market, the value of iron, nickel, and gold would collapse worldwide. The economists are not amused.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Resource Assessment Lead
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_psyche.dds

### space_race_colony_events.9
- **Title:** Colony: 2 Pallas
- **Description:** Pallas is an oddity: a carbon-rich proto-planet with an extreme axial tilt of 84 degrees, making it spin nearly on its side. Its dark surface is rich in carbonaceous material: the building blocks of organic chemistry and composite manufacturing feedstock. The unusual tilt creates bizarre seasonal lighting conditions that will challenge our habitat designers.
- **Flavor:** \"It rolls through space at an angle no one can explain. Our orbital insertion was the most creative flying this program has ever attempted.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Navigation Officer
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_pallas.dds

### space_race_colony_events.10
- **Title:** Colony: 10 Hygiea
- **Description:** Nearly spherical and dark as coal, Hygiea is the fourth largest asteroid and the largest member of its own collisional family. Its surface is rich in carbonaceous material and volatiles: water ice, ammonia, methane: making it a natural supply depot for settlements deeper in the belt. The low surface gravity (about 0.003g) makes landing and launch trivially easy.
- **Flavor:** \"Dark, round, and rich in carbon. Not glamorous, but the colony that makes the fuel that runs the fleet.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Fuel Processing Director
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_hygiea.dds

### space_race_colony_events.11
- **Title:** Colony: Io
- **Description:** No world in the solar system is more hostile to settlement than Io. Jupiter's tidal forces flex our landing site by up to 100 meters with each orbit. Over 400 active volcanoes blanket the moon in sulfur dioxide frost and fresh lava flows. The radiation environment would kill an unshielded human in hours. And yet, Io offers something no other world can: virtually unlimited tidal energy and a sulfur feedstock for industrial chemistry.
- **Flavor:** \"The ground shakes. The sky glows with sulfur. Geysers erupt without warning. And yet — here we are, building something permanent on the most violent surface in the solar system.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Station Commander
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_io.dds

### space_race_colony_events.12
- **Title:** Colony: Europa
- **Description:** Beneath Europa's cracked ice shell lies a global saltwater ocean, kept liquid by tidal heating. This ocean contains roughly twice the water of all Earth's oceans combined. The ice surface is geologically young: constantly resurfaced by cryovolcanic activity: and the lineae suggest material exchange between surface and ocean. If life exists elsewhere in our solar system, Europa's ocean floor vents are the most likely place.
- **Flavor:** \"Beneath the ice, an ocean older than life on Earth. Every sensor we lower makes us hold our breath.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Astrobiology Team Lead
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_europa.dds

### space_race_colony_events.13
- **Title:** Colony: Ganymede
- **Description:** Ganymede is the largest moon in the solar system: bigger than Mercury: and the only moon with its own magnetosphere. This intrinsic magnetic field, though weak, creates a pocket of reduced radiation within Jupiter's lethal belts. Combined with its size, subsurface ocean, and silicate-rich surface, Ganymede is the natural capital of the Jovian system.
- **Flavor:** \"Its own magnetic field. Its own geology. Ganymede is less a moon and more a planet that never left home.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Colony Administrator
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_ganymede.dds

### space_race_colony_events.14
- **Title:** Colony: Callisto
- **Description:** Callisto lies just outside Jupiter's main radiation belts, making it the safest of the Galilean moons for long-term habitation. Its ancient, heavily cratered surface has not been resurfaced in billions of years. The lack of geological activity means stable foundations, and its distance from Jupiter allows for relatively simple communications relay geometry to the inner solar system.
- **Flavor:** \"The boring moon, they call it. No volcanoes, no oceans, no drama. Just rock, ice, and the lowest radiation of any Jovian satellite. Perfect.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Radiation Safety Officer
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_callisto.dds

### space_race_colony_events.15
- **Title:** Colony: Himalia
- **Description:** Himalia, an irregular moon captured long ago from a heliocentric orbit, sits 11 million kilometers from Jupiter: well beyond the punishing radiation belts that endanger the Galilean moons. At roughly 150 kilometers across, it offers negligible gravity but a stable platform far from the electromagnetic storms closer in. A small crew and a large telescope array could accomplish extraordinary things here.
- **Flavor:** \"Eleven million kilometers from Jupiter. Far enough to be safe, close enough to matter. A quiet perch from which to watch the giant.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Observatory Director
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_himalia.dds

### space_race_colony_events.16
- **Title:** Colony: Amalthea
- **Description:** Amalthea orbits within Jupiter's gossamer ring: close enough to the gas giant that tidal forces have stretched it into an irregular, reddish potato shape. The radiation flux here is extreme, but the proximity to Jupiter's magnetosphere makes it an ideal platform for high-energy physics research. The ring particles streaming past the station offer a natural laboratory for studying plasma dynamics.
- **Flavor:** \"Red dust, battered craters, and radiation that would kill you in hours without shielding. But the view of Jupiter filling half the sky — that makes it worth it.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], EVA Team Lead
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_amalthea.dds

### space_race_colony_events.17
- **Title:** Colony: Venus Cloud Habitat
- **Description:** At 50 kilometers altitude in Venus's atmosphere, conditions are startlingly Earth-like: one atmosphere of pressure, temperatures between 0 and 50 degrees Celsius, and protection from cosmic radiation by the thick atmosphere above. Our aerostatic habitat: part balloon, part sealed structure: floats in this temperate zone. Below lies a hellscape of 460°C surface temperatures and crushing pressure; above, sulfuric acid clouds. Between them, we have found a home.
- **Flavor:** \"Fifty kilometers up, the temperature is pleasant, the pressure is breathable, and there is acid rain above and a furnace below. We call it paradise.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Habitat Chief Engineer
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_venus_cloud.dds

### space_race_colony_events.18
- **Title:** Colony: Mercury
- **Description:** Mercury's poles offer a remarkable paradox: permanently shadowed craters cold enough to harbor ice, within line of sight of surfaces receiving the most intense sunlight in the solar system. Our polar base straddles this boundary: solar collectors on the sunward rim generating power, while the habitat nestles in perpetual shadow. The concentrated solar flux makes Mercury the ideal site for beamed power transmission to other settlements.
- **Flavor:** \"Dawn and dusk last for weeks here. We live in the terminator zone — one foot in fire, one in ice, and a narrow strip of the tolerable in between.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Thermal Systems Engineer
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_mercury.dds

### space_race_colony_events.19
- **Title:** Colony: Titan
- **Description:** Titan is the only moon with a thick atmosphere: 1.5x Earth's surface pressure, mostly nitrogen. Its surface is sculpted by methane rain, carved by ethane rivers, and dotted with hydrocarbon lakes. Kraken Mare, the largest, covers more area than the Caspian Sea. At -179°C, the chemistry is exotic but energetic: tholin compounds in the haze hint at prebiotic processes operating on entirely alien biochemistry.
- **Flavor:** \"It rains here. Methane rain, on methane lakes, under an orange sky thicker than Earth's. If you squint, you could almost pretend it's home.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Atmospheric Researcher
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_titan.dds

### space_race_colony_events.20
- **Title:** Colony: Enceladus
- **Description:** Enceladus punches far above its weight. Only 500 kilometers across, it harbors a global subsurface ocean kept warm by tidal forces. Geysers erupt from the tiger-stripe fissures at its south pole, spraying water ice, organic molecules, and silica nanoparticles into space. Cassini flew through these plumes and detected molecular hydrogen: a potential energy source for microbial life. Our colony perches beside the fissures, sampling what the moon offers freely.
- **Flavor:** \"The geysers are how we found the ocean. And the ocean is why we came. What else might be down there — that is why we stay.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Subsurface Exploration Lead
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_enceladus.dds

### space_race_colony_events.21
- **Title:** Colony: Rhea
- **Description:** Saturn's second-largest moon is a quiet, icy body without the drama of its siblings. No geysers, no thick atmosphere, no extreme tidal heating. What Rhea offers is stability: a known, predictable surface of water ice and rock, moderate surface gravity, and a position well-suited for servicing missions throughout the Saturnian system. Sometimes the most valuable real estate is simply the most reliable.
- **Flavor:** \"No surprises, no eruptions, no subsurface oceans. Just ice and rock and a reliable platform a billion kilometers from Earth. Sometimes boring is exactly what you need.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Station Operations Director
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_saturn_icy_moon.dds

### space_race_colony_events.22
- **Title:** Colony: Mimas
- **Description:** Mimas is instantly recognizable: the Herschel crater, 130 kilometers wide, covers nearly a third of the moon's diameter, giving it an uncanny resemblance to science fiction's most famous space station. The crater's central peak rises 6 kilometers from the floor. Inside this ready-made amphitheater, our engineers have found both shelter from micrometeorites and a natural foundation for pressure domes.
- **Flavor:** \"They said it looks like a certain space station from an old film. Having been here in person, I can confirm: nobody is laughing.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Survey Team Leader
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_saturn_icy_moon.dds

### space_race_colony_events.23
- **Title:** Colony: Iapetus
- **Description:** Iapetus refuses to be ordinary. One hemisphere is as dark as coal; the other, bright as snow. A massive equatorial ridge: up to 20 kilometers high: girdles the moon like the seam on a tennis ball. No satisfactory explanation exists for either feature. Our colony is positioned on the boundary between dark and light terrain, with the ridge visible as a wall on the horizon.
- **Flavor:** \"Half the moon is white ice, the other half is dark as coal, with a mountain range running along the equator like a belt. Nobody has explained any of this.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Planetary Scientist
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_saturn_icy_moon.dds

### space_race_colony_events.24
- **Title:** Colony: Titania
- **Description:** Titania, the largest of Uranus's moons, is a world of great scarps and ancient canyons: evidence of a violent tectonic past. The Messina Chasmata stretches for hundreds of kilometers across the surface. With Uranus tilted on its side, Titania experiences 42-year-long seasons of continuous sunlight followed by 42 years of darkness. Our colony must be truly self-sufficient.
- **Flavor:** \"Forty-two years of daylight, then forty-two years of darkness. You plan your career around the seasons here.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Base Commander
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_uranus_moon.dds

### space_race_colony_events.25
- **Title:** Colony: Oberon
- **Description:** Oberon, the outermost major moon of Uranus, is a battered ball of ice and rock. Its dark, ancient surface is marked by impact craters and what may be cryovolcanic flows on the floors of the largest basins. At nearly 3 billion kilometers from the Sun, our colonists experience a solitude unmatched by any other permanent settlement. The round-trip communication delay with Earth exceeds 5 hours.
- **Flavor:** \"The most distant permanently crewed outpost in history. Mail takes nearly three hours to arrive, and just as long for our reply to get back to Earth. You learn patience, or you learn to go home.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Communications Officer
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_uranus_moon.dds

### space_race_colony_events.26
- **Title:** Colony: Miranda
- **Description:** Miranda is the geological puzzle of the Uranian system. Despite being only 470 kilometers across, it displays terrain that should not exist on a body this small: Verona Rupes, a 20-kilometer cliff: the tallest in the solar system: and chevron-shaped ridged regions called coronae that suggest the moon was shattered and reassembled, or experienced extreme tidal heating in its past.
- **Flavor:** \"A cliff twenty kilometers high. You could jump off and have ten minutes of freefall before landing. Not that anyone has tried. Yet.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Geological Survey Lead
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_uranus_moon.dds

### space_race_colony_events.27
- **Title:** Colony: Ariel
- **Description:** Ariel has the youngest and brightest surface of any Uranian moon. Networks of fault valleys and smooth plains suggest relatively recent cryovolcanic resurfacing: perhaps CO₂ or ammonia-water eruptions in the geologically recent past. This level of activity on a small icy body billions of kilometers from the Sun challenges our models of planetary geology. Understanding it could reshape our understanding of how small worlds evolve.
- **Flavor:** \"The youngest and brightest face among the moons of Uranus. The ice here is fresh, the canyons are sharp, and the geology is still active.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Research Outpost Director
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_uranus_moon.dds

### space_race_colony_events.28
- **Title:** Colony: Triton
- **Description:** Triton is Neptune's largest moon and almost certainly a captured Kuiper Belt object: it orbits retrograde, the only large moon in the solar system to do so. Active nitrogen geysers jet dark material 8 kilometers into the thin atmosphere. The surface temperature of -235°C makes it one of the coldest bodies ever visited. Despite the extreme conditions, Triton's unique origin makes it a scientific treasure and a natural gateway to the Kuiper Belt.
- **Flavor:** \"It orbits the wrong way — a captured wanderer from the Kuiper Belt. Geysers of nitrogen erupt from its surface. Neptune looms overhead like a blue god.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Planetology Chief
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_triton.dds

### space_race_colony_events.29
- **Title:** Colony: Proteus
- **Description:** Proteus orbits close to Neptune: so close that tidal forces have stretched it to the limit of what an icy body can sustain without collapsing into a sphere. Dark and irregular, it is a useful platform for studying Neptune's atmosphere, ring arcs, and magnetosphere at close range. The proximity does mean dealing with Neptune's radiation environment, though it is mild compared to Jupiter's.
- **Flavor:** \"An irregular lump of rock and ice hanging on the edge of Neptune's system. Not beautiful. Not dramatic. But it is ours.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Outpost Administrator
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_neptune_outpost.dds

### space_race_colony_events.30
- **Title:** Colony: Pluto-Charon
- **Description:** Pluto and Charon orbit each other as a true binary system: tidally locked, always showing the same face. Pluto's nitrogen glaciers flow slowly across Sputnik Planitia, a 1,000-kilometer basin of frozen nitrogen ice. The thin atmosphere freezes and refreezes in a centuries-long cycle. Charon's scarred surface tells of ancient cryovolcanism. Our dual-body colony spans both worlds, connected by regular shuttle service across the 19,570-kilometer gap.
- **Flavor:** \"A binary world, each partner tidally locked to the other, dancing through the dark. We built the station in the space between them.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Orbital Mechanics Engineer
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_deep_kuiper.dds

### space_race_colony_events.31
- **Title:** Colony: Eris
- **Description:** Eris, the most massive known dwarf planet, orbits at three times Pluto's distance. The round-trip light delay to Earth exceeds 26 hours. Our colonists must operate with a degree of autonomy unmatched by any other settlement. Eris's small moon Dysnomia provides a convenient observing platform. This colony is above all a test of self-sufficiency: if we can sustain human life here, we can sustain it anywhere in the solar system.
- **Flavor:** \"So far away that our transmissions to Earth take thirteen hours. By the time they hear our news, it is already yesterday's triumph.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Communications Relay Operator
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_deep_kuiper.dds

### space_race_colony_events.32
- **Title:** Colony: Makemake
- **Description:** Makemake's surface is coated in methane and ethane ice that shifts in spectral properties as the dwarf planet's elliptical orbit carries it nearer and farther from the distant Sun. With no known atmosphere and no confirmed moons for years after its discovery: until tiny S/2015 (136472) 1 was spotted: Makemake offers a pristine laboratory for studying the primordial composition of the outer solar system.
- **Flavor:** \"Frozen since the birth of the solar system. Every core sample is a time capsule from four and a half billion years ago. We are the first to open them.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Chief Geochemist
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_deep_kuiper.dds

### space_race_colony_events.33
- **Title:** Colony: Haumea
- **Description:** Haumea rotates once every four hours: the fastest rotation of any known large body in the solar system. This furious spin has stretched it into an elongated ellipsoid, wider than it is tall. It also possesses a dark ring system, one of the few ring systems known around a body other than the giant planets. Two small moons, Hi'iaka and Namaka, orbit amid the ring debris. Our colony platform must account for the rapid rotation in everything from docking to power generation.
- **Flavor:** \"Egg-shaped, spinning faster than any world this size should, and wearing its own ring of debris. Even the physicists shake their heads.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Rotational Dynamics Specialist
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_deep_kuiper.dds

### space_race_colony_events.34
- **Title:** Colony: Sedna
- **Description:** Sedna occupies one of the most extreme orbits known: a 11,400-year ellipse that carries it from 76 AU at perihelion to over 900 AU at aphelion: deep into the inner Oort Cloud. We have caught it near perihelion, when it is: by its standards: close. Our outpost here is the most distant permanent human habitation, farther from the Sun than any settlement has ever been or likely will be for generations. The Sun is barely distinguishable from the brighter stars.
- **Flavor:** \"Eleven thousand years to orbit the Sun once. We are the furthest humans from Earth. The next star is still unfathomably far. But we are here.\"\n\n— [SCOPE.sCharacter('flavor_speaker').GetFullNameNoFormatting], Expedition Commander
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/colony_sedna.dds

### space_race_events.5
- **Title:** Where the Eagle Shall Land
- **Description:** The lunar landing site selection committee has narrowed the options to four candidates. Shackleton Crater near the south pole offers access to permanently shadowed regions that may contain water ice: scientifically invaluable but extremely hazardous. The Equatorial Plain offers well-mapped terrain and reliable conditions. The Sea of Tranquility, first mapped by early telescopes, offers a flat expanse ideal for a symbolically powerful landing. And the far side of the Moon, radio-shielded from Earth, is perfect for deep-space observation but demands autonomous navigation.
- **Flavor:** \"Shackleton is a geologist's dream and a pilot's nightmare. The crater rim gets sunlight, but one degree off course and you're in permanent shadow at minus 170 Celsius.\"\n\n- Landing Site Review Board\n\n\"The equatorial sites are boring. Safe, yes. But boring. And boring doesn't win the space race.\"\n\n- Program Chief Scientist

### space_race_events.41

- **Description:** Cost analysis of the current mission profile is sobering. Every kilogram delivered to the lunar or Martian surface costs orders of magnitude more than its Earth-side equivalent. The program's economics depend entirely on reducing the cost per kilogram to orbit.
- **Flavor:** \"Tsiolkovsky's equation doesn't negotiate. You either throw more mass out the back or you find a way around the equation entirely.\"\n\n- Senior Propulsion Engineer\n\n\"The elevator changes everything: if we have one. If we don't, it's chemical rockets all the way, and the budget bleeds.\"\n\n- Program Financial Controller

### space_race_events.43

- **Description:** Long-duration habitation requires a life-support system that recycles nearly everything: air, water, and waste: with minimal resupply from Earth. Current recycling rates hover around 90%, but sustained habitation demands 98% or better. The engineering challenge is as much biological as mechanical.
- **Flavor:** \"A submarine can stay sealed for six months. We need to stay sealed for years. The difference isn't engineering: it's ecology. We're building a biosphere in a tin can.\"\n\n- Life Support Systems Lead\n\n\"The algae reactors are the lungs. The bacterial processors are the kidneys. If either fails, everyone dies together. No pressure.\"\n\n- Lead Bioengineer, with a humorless smile

### space_race_events.16

- **Flavor:** \"Separation: negative. Negative sep. We have a tumble. Flight, we have a tumble.\"\n\n- Range Safety Officer, final transmission before vehicle destruction\n\n\"All those engines worked perfectly. It was eight bolts that didn't.\"\n\n- Chief Engineer, in the review board

### space_race_events.18
- **Title:** The Paper Trail
- **Description:** Investigative journalists have uncovered evidence of systematic cost overruns, falsified safety certifications, and a culture of schedule pressure that silenced engineers who raised concerns. The revelations threaten to erode public confidence in the entire space program just as it reaches a critical phase.
- **Flavor:** \"The reports were filed. The warnings were given. Management chose the launch date over the data.\"\n\n- Anonymous whistleblower, quoted in the morning papers\n\n\"We will find out exactly what happened, and heads will roll.\"\n\n- Parliamentary Committee Chair
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/program_scandal_newsroom.dds

### space_race_events.19
- **Title:** Shadows on the Launchpad
- **Description:** Anomalous tool marks on a critical fuel line. An access log showing unauthorized entries at 3 AM. A suspiciously precise failure that destroyed exactly the component most difficult to replace. Intelligence officials suspect deliberate sabotage: perhaps from a rival power that cannot afford to see us succeed.
- **Flavor:** \"Coincidence has a pattern, and this pattern spells intent. Someone wanted this vehicle to fail.\"\n\n- Head of Program Security\n\n\"Or we just had a bad batch of titanium fittings. Let's not start an international incident over metallurgy.\"\n\n- Chief Engineer, urging caution
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/sabotage_investigation.dds

### space_race_events.21
- **Title:** The Missing Parts
- **Description:** A critical shipment of precision-machined components has been delayed indefinitely. The supplier cites raw material shortages and unexpected demand, but the result is the same: our integration schedule just slipped by weeks. Without these parts, the vehicle sits incomplete on the assembly floor.
- **Flavor:** \"You can't fly to space on promises. You need machined titanium, and right now there's a six-week backlog at every forge on the continent.\"\n\n- Program Logistics Director
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/mission_delay_hangar.dds

### space_race_events.22
- **Title:** Grounded by the Sky
- **Description:** A massive storm system has settled over the launch site with no sign of departure. Upper-level wind shear readings exceed every safety margin in the book. The vehicle stands ready on the pad, fully fueled and flight-capable: waiting for weather that refuses to cooperate. Each day of delay costs money and, more critically, narrows the orbital mechanics window.
- **Flavor:** \"Nature doesn't care about our launch schedule. The jet stream is where it wants to be, and we will wait.\"\n\n- Range Weather Officer, morning briefing
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/mission_delay_hangar.dds

### space_race_events.23
- **Title:** Two Characters
- **Description:** A simulation run caught it: a floating-point rounding error in the attitude control subroutine. In normal operations it would accumulate unnoticed over hours, but during a critical burn sequence it would compound into a navigation error of several degrees: enough to miss a planetary target entirely or, worse, point the main engine in the wrong direction.
- **Flavor:** \"Line 4,217 of module AOCS_PRIMARY. A less-than that should have been a less-than-or-equal-to. Two characters, and it would have cost us the mission.\"\n\n- Lead Software Engineer, looking very pale
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/computer_error_cockpit.dds

### space_race_events.24
- **Title:** The Price of the Stars
- **Description:** The Budget Committee has summoned the program director for testimony. With domestic priorities competing for funds and no tangible return yet visible to the average voter, influential legislators are questioning whether the nation can justify the expense. The program's future hangs on a hearing room presentation.
- **Flavor:** \"Senator, I understand the cost concerns. But I would remind the committee that our rivals are not holding budget hearings: they are building rockets.\"\n\n- Program Director, opening statement
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/budget_hearing_congress.dds

### space_race_events.25
- **Title:** Microns of Failure
- **Description:** Quality inspection has flagged an entire batch of turbopump impellers: the tolerances are outside specification by microns, but in a system operating at thousands of RPM and extreme temperatures, microns matter. Every unit in the last three months of production must be pulled and re-inspected. Some are already installed in vehicles being prepared for launch.
- **Flavor:** \"Microns. We're talking about the width of a bacterium. And it's enough to shatter a turbopump at full thrust.\"\n\n- Chief Quality Inspector, examining the impeller under magnification
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/mission_delay_hangar.dds

### space_race_events.26
- **Title:** When Politics Reaches Orbit
- **Description:** A sudden deterioration in international relations has disrupted the space program's operations. Foreign-sourced components are stuck in customs. Tracking station access in allied nations is now politically sensitive. Technical exchange agreements signed in better times are being quietly frozen by nervous diplomats.
- **Flavor:** \"We had a handshake agreement with their space agency: data sharing, tracking support, the works. Now their foreign ministry won't return our calls.\"\n\n- International Cooperation Director
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/budget_hearing_congress.dds

### space_race_events.70
- **Title:** Inferno at the Launch Complex
- **Description:** A catastrophic explosion has torn through the primary launch complex. The detonation occurred during a routine fueling procedure, sending a column of fire hundreds of meters into the sky. Emergency crews found the pad reduced to twisted wreckage, and the surrounding support structures sustained severe damage. Hundreds of engineers and technicians working in the blast radius did not survive.
- **Flavor:** \"The sound reached the control room before the shockwave did. Then the windows blew in. By the time we pulled ourselves off the floor and looked at the monitors, there was nothing left to monitor.\"\n\n- Launch Director, in the aftermath
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/launch_pad_explosion.dds

### space_race_events.71
- **Title:** Silent Capsule
- **Description:** During a routine pressure integrity test of the crew capsule, the primary seal failed without warning. The capsule depressurized in seconds. The test crew: experienced engineers performing a standard checkout procedure: had no time to reach emergency equipment. An entire team of our brightest minds, lost in an instant to a failed gasket.
- **Flavor:** \"They were the best we had. Not astronauts: the engineers who made astronauts possible. They died in a chair on the ground, doing the job nobody else could do.\"\n\n- Program Director, addressing the press
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/capsule_seal_failure.dds

### space_race_events.72
- **Title:** Fire in the Assembly Building
- **Description:** A fire broke out in the main integration facility during the night shift. Quick-thinking technicians activated fire suppression systems before the blaze could reach the fuel storage, but the damage to sensitive equipment and clean-room environments is extensive. No casualties, but the repair timeline will slow the program.
- **Flavor:** \"The clean room is anything but. Soot on every surface, water damage from the suppression system, and the centrifuge is a write-off. We'll be rebuilding test capability for months.\"\n\n- Facility Manager, surveying the damage
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/assembly_building_fire.dds

### space_race_events.73
- **Title:** Stars and Scandals
- **Description:** An investigative journalist has published a devastating exposé of cost overruns and financial mismanagement within the space program. Contracts awarded to connected firms at inflated prices, expense accounts that defy belief, and schedule milestones fabricated to justify continued funding. Public trust in the program has been severely damaged.
- **Flavor:** \"The public was told that every dollar went to the stars. It turns out quite a few of those dollars went to beach houses and luxury automobiles.\"\n\n- Investigative Report, lead paragraph\n\n\"These are teething problems of a program growing faster than its oversight. We need reform, not cancellation.\"\n\n- Space Program Advisory Board Chair
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/program_scandal_newsroom.dds

### space_race_events.74
- **Title:** An Unexpected Breakthrough
- **Description:** A team of engineers working on a perplexing propulsion problem has achieved a fundamental breakthrough. Their novel approach to thrust vectoring and fuel efficiency dramatically exceeds theoretical predictions. If validated, this innovation could revolutionize the program's capabilities and accelerate the current mission timeline.
- **Flavor:** \"We were trying to fix a combustion instability problem. Instead we found a way to extract thirty percent more impulse from the same propellant mass. Sometimes the best discoveries happen when you're looking for something else entirely.\"\n\n- Lead Propulsion Engineer
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/engineering_breakthrough_lab.dds

### space_race_events.75
- **Title:** The Parts That Didn't Come
- **Description:** Critical precision components: guidance gyroscopes, radiation-hardened electronics, and specialty alloys: have failed to arrive on schedule. The suppliers report production delays caused by competing defense contracts and raw material shortages. Without these components, major integration milestones cannot proceed.
- **Flavor:** \"We can build a rocket that reaches orbit, but we can't build the bearings for the gyroscope that points it there. Three companies on Earth make them to our specifications, and all three are six months behind.\"\n\n- Supply Chain Director, in a progress review meeting
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/mission_delay_hangar.dds

### space_race_events.76
- **Title:** Program Discontinued
- **Description:** With the space program facilities no longer operational, [ROOT.GetCountry.GetAdjective] ambitions beyond Earth have been shelved. The scientists and engineers who dedicated themselves to the mission now seek new assignments, and the vast [concept_infrastructure] built for the program sits idle.
- **Flavor:** #italic The stars will have to wait.#!
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/program_cancelled_empty.dds

### space_race_events.80
- **Title:** Who Flies First?
- **Description:** As our orbital program nears readiness, a fundamental question must be answered: who will we send into space? A civilian volunteer would demonstrate that space belongs to all humanity. A military test pilot brings discipline and familiarity with high-performance vehicles. Or we could send a scientist, turning the flight into a research mission from the very first orbit.
- **Flavor:** \"Any of them could fly it. The question is what message we want to send to the world when the hatch opens and our astronaut waves.\"\n\n— Program Selection Committee Chair
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/space_race.dds

### space_race_events.81
- **Title:** Where Shall We Send the Probe?
- **Description:** Our probe is ready for its journey beyond Earth orbit. Three targets have been proposed. Venus, shrouded in clouds, could reveal whether a runaway greenhouse effect awaits our own world. Mars, with its ancient riverbeds and polar ice, is the most likely candidate for past life. The asteroid belt offers navigational and prospecting data that could accelerate future off-world industry.
- **Flavor:** \"Venus will teach us about our past. Mars will teach us about our future. The asteroids will teach us about our bank accounts.\"\n\n— Planetary Science Advisory Panel
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/space_race.dds

### space_race_events.82
- **Title:** The Purpose of the Base
- **Description:** With a permanent lunar presence becoming reality, we must decide the base's primary mission. A scientific outpost would advance pure research and attract international collaboration. An industrial facility could begin extracting helium-3 and rare minerals. A military installation would provide unmatched strategic observation capabilities and serve as a staging point for force projection.
- **Flavor:** \"A laboratory, a mine, or a fortress. Each choice shapes not just what we do on the Moon, but who we become as a spacefaring nation.\"\n\n— Lunar Planning Commission
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/space_station.dds

### space_race_events.83
- **Title:** The Mars Strategy
- **Description:** The Mars mission architecture must be decided. A direct landing puts boots on the surface fastest but carries enormous risk. An orbital-first approach establishes a station in Mars orbit before attempting a landing, building experience methodically. Sending robotic precursors to prepare a landing site and cache supplies is safest but slowest, and may allow rivals to land first.
- **Flavor:** \"Direct is bold. Orbital-first is smart. Robotic precursors are safe. We can only pick one, and whichever we choose defines a generation.\"\n\n— Mars Architecture Review Board
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/space_station.dds

## surveillance_events.txt

### surveillance_events.1
- **Title:** The Whistleblower
- **Description:** A government insider has leaked classified documents revealing the extent of state surveillance on ordinary citizens. The revelations have sparked outrage among civil liberties advocates and a fierce debate about security versus privacy.
- **Flavor:** The leaked files filled fourteen boxes. A clerk in the ministry had been copying them for six months before anyone noticed.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/whistleblower_documents.dds

### surveillance_events.2
- **Title:** The Data Breach
- **Description:** A massive data breach has exposed the personal information of millions of citizens. Private correspondence, financial records, and intimate details are now public. The government faces a reckoning.
- **Flavor:** Names, addresses, medical records, private correspondence — all of it posted on a public server. The government learned about it from the newspapers.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/data_breach_screens.dds

### surveillance_events.3
- **Title:** Hacker Collective Attack
- **Description:** A sophisticated hacker collective has breached government systems, leaking classified data to the public. The leaked documents reveal the extent of domestic surveillance programs. The hackers claim to be freedom fighters; the state calls them criminals.
- **Flavor:** The hackers published everything: surveillance logs, internal memos, the personal browsing history of three senior officials. The public reaction was divided between outrage at the surveillance and amusement at the browsing history.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/data_breach_screens.dds

### surveillance_events.4
- **Title:** Predictive Policing
- **Description:** AI-powered systems can now predict crimes before they happen, identifying potential offenders through behavioral analysis. Law enforcement is eager to deploy the technology, but civil liberties groups warn of a dystopian future where citizens are punished for crimes they have not yet committed.
- **Flavor:** The system flagged two hundred and twelve individuals as potential offenders last quarter. Thirty-seven were arrested. None had yet committed a crime.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/predictive_policing_ai.dds

### surveillance_events.5
- **Title:** Foreign Cyber-Espionage
- **Description:** Intelligence services have uncovered evidence that a rival power has been conducting systematic cyber-espionage against our government and critical [concept_infrastructure]. The breach is extensive and has compromised sensitive data.
- **Flavor:** The breach was discovered on a Monday. By Thursday, the analysts had mapped its extent. By Friday, they wished they hadn't.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/cyber_espionage_network.dds

## treaty_article_events.txt

### treaty_article_events.1

- **Description:** Our intelligence partners have intercepted communications revealing an imminent terror plot on our soil. Thanks to our information-sharing agreement with [SCOPE.sCountry('intel_partner').GetName], the conspirators were identified before they could act.
- **Flavor:** \"The intercept came in at three in the morning. Forty minutes later, every suspect was under surveillance.\"\n\n\"And if we hadn't had the agreement?\"\n\n\"Then we'd be reading about it in the newspapers instead.\"
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/intelligence_sharing_success.dds

### treaty_article_events.2
- **Title:** The Dead Drop
- **Description:** A critical intelligence report from [SCOPE.sCountry('intel_partner').GetName] was delayed by bureaucratic confusion and interdepartmental rivalry. By the time the warning reached the right desk, the damage was done. Our intelligence-sharing pact failed us when it mattered most.
- **Flavor:** \"The file sat in a translation queue for eleven days. Eleven days.\"\n\n\"Somebody will answer for this.\"\n\n\"Somebody always does. Never the right somebody.\"
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/intelligence_dead_drop.dds

- **Description:** The protections afforded to minority communities under recent treaty [Concept('concept_obligation', 'obligations')] have borne unexpected fruit. - **Flavor:** \"Have you read the new collection? Extraordinary stuff.\"\n\n\"I hear the Royal Academy wants to commission a series.\"\n\n\"Three years ago they couldn't get published. Funny how that works.\"

Pamphlets circulate denouncing the government as traitors to the nation, and ugly incidents are being reported in several provinces.
- **Flavor:** \"They say we're selling the country to foreigners. That the old ways are dying.\"\n\n\"The old ways include burning people's homes.\"\n\n\"Try explaining that to a mob.\"

### treaty_article_events.5

- **Description:** The senior officer corps is barely containing its rage. Our nuclear disarmament [Concept('concept_obligation', 'obligations')] have stripped away the ultimate guarantee of national security, and the generals want the government to know exactly how they feel about it.
- **Flavor:** \"The Field Marshal threw his medals on the table. Said he didn't earn them to watch the country disarm itself.\"\n\n\"And the Defense Minister?\"\n\n\"Pretended to be on a telephone call.\"

- **Description:** Combined military exercises with [SCOPE.sCountry('exercise_partner').GetName] have exceeded all expectations. Our officers have returned with fresh tactical insights and a profound respect for their counterparts' methods.
- **Flavor:** \"Their field engineers bridged a river in twenty minutes. Twenty minutes! Our best time was forty-five.\"\n\n\"What did the Colonel say?\"\n\n\"He said we're going to learn how to do it in fifteen.\"

- **Description:** The foreign-funded education initiative is producing remarkable results. A new generation of students is emerging with skills and perspectives that promise to transform our economy and society.
- **Flavor:** \"The village school had forty pupils last year. This year, one hundred and twelve.\"\n\n\"And the exam results?\"\n\n\"Three of them qualified for the national engineering program. First time ever from that district.\"

### treaty_article_events.8

- **Flavor:** \"Every month those facilities sit idle, we fall further behind.\"\n\n\"Behind whom? That's precisely the point of the freeze.\"\n\n\"You can't freeze ambition. Only delay it.\"

### treaty_article_events.9

- **Flavor:** \"The foreign advisors now outnumber our own staff in three departments.\"\n\n\"Do they take orders from us or from their embassy?\"\n\n\"Does it matter, as long as the funding continues?\"\n\n\"It will matter. Eventually.\"

Their artists exhibit in our galleries, our writers are being translated in their universities, and the world is taking notice of this flourishing partnership.

Protests have been organized, and several cultural institutions have faced pressure to cancel planned events.

- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/nationalist_backlash_flags.dds

## un_events.txt

### un_events.1
- **Title:** The United Nations Charter
- **Description:** In the aftermath of another devastating conflict, the nations of the world have drafted a charter for a new international body - the United Nations. [ROOT.GetCountry.GetName] has been invited to sign as a founding member. Membership promises a seat at the table of global governance, but carries [Concept('concept_obligation', 'obligations')]: international courts, collective security, and the subordination of national interests to the common good.
- **Flavor:** The ambassador set down his pen and stared at the document. 'Do you know,' he said to no one in particular, 'how many treaties have promised to end all wars?'\n\n'Every single one of them,' his aide replied. 'And yet here we are, drafting another.'\n\n'Yes. And yet here we are.'
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/un_charter_signing.dds

### un_events.2
- **Title:** General Assembly Condemns Aggression
- **Description:** The General Assembly has convened an emergency session to address the military aggression of [SCOPE.sCountry('condemned_country').GetName]. Delegates from around the world are calling for a formal condemnation resolution, and [ROOT.GetCountry.GetName] must decide how to vote.
- **Flavor:** The delegate from [SCOPE.sCountry('defender_country').GetName] rose to speak, his hands trembling. 'My country has no army,' he said. 'We have no bombs, no warships, no leverage of any kind. We have only this chamber and the hope that words spoken here still carry some weight.'\n\nThe gallery fell silent. For a moment, the institution almost believed in itself.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/un_assembly_hall_vote.dds

### un_events.3
- **Title:** Declaration of Universal Human Rights
- **Description:** A Universal Declaration of Human Rights has been proposed at the United Nations, establishing fundamental freedoms as the common standard for all peoples and nations. Ratifying it would signal our commitment to the international order, though some provisions may conflict with domestic policy.
- **Flavor:** 'Article One,' the chairwoman read aloud. 'All human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights.' She looked up from the page. 'Does any delegation object?'\n\nA long silence. Then, from the back row, a dry voice: 'To the sentiment, Madam Chair, no one objects. To the enforcement - that is where the arguments begin.'
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/human_rights_declaration.dds

### un_events.4
- **Title:** Peacekeeping Mission Authorized
- **Description:** The Security Council has authorized a peacekeeping mission in the conflict zone involving [SCOPE.sCountry('peacekeeping_target').GetName]. As a committed contributor, [ROOT.GetCountry.GetName] has been called upon to provide troops for the operation.
- **Flavor:** The colonel studied the deployment orders and folded them carefully into his breast pocket. 'Blue helmets,' he said to his adjutant. 'Rules of engagement that would embarrass a traffic warden. No authority to fire unless fired upon, and even then, only if committee approves.'\n\nHe paused at the door. 'Still. Someone has to stand between the guns.'
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/peacekeeping_deployment.dds

### un_events.5
- **Title:** Enforcing the Sanctions Regime
- **Description:** The [concept_un_sanctions] against [SCOPE.sCountry('sanctioned_country').GetName] are now in effect, but enforcement requires active cooperation from member states. Strict compliance will hurt our own trade routes; the alternative is to quietly circumvent the very institution we helped create.
- **Flavor:** 'The manifest says fertilizer,' the customs inspector said, turning the page with exaggerated slowness. 'Quite a lot of fertilizer.' He looked up. 'For a country with no farms.'\n\nThe shipping agent smiled and slid an envelope across the desk. 'A clerical error. I'm sure you understand.'
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/sanctions_cargo_inspection.dds

### un_events.6

- **Description:** A growing coalition of nations is demanding reform of the Security Council. The current structure, with its permanent members and [concept_un_veto] power, is seen as increasingly unrepresentative. As a [concept_great_power], [ROOT.GetCountry.GetName] must decide whether to champion reform or defend the status quo.
- **Flavor:** 'We are told this body represents the world,' the ambassador said, adjusting his spectacles. 'And yet the same five nations have held the same five seats since before half the countries in this room existed.'\n\nThe delegate from the permanent member state glanced at his papers. 'The matter has been raised before,' he replied. 'The committee will take it under advisement.'\n\nIt had been taken under advisement eleven times.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/un_assembly_hall_vote.dds

### un_events.7
- **Title:** Humanitarian Crisis Demands Response
- **Description:** Reports from [SCOPE.sCountry('crisis_country').GetName] paint a dire picture - widespread famine, displacement, and suffering on a massive scale. The United Nations has issued an urgent appeal for humanitarian assistance from member states.
- **Flavor:** The relief coordinator set down the telegram and pressed her palms flat against the desk. 'Three hundred thousand displaced,' she said. 'That is the confirmed figure. The actual number is anyone's guess.'\n\nHer aide handed her a coffee, gone cold. 'How much can we send?'\n\n'The question is not how much we can send. The question is how much we are willing to be seen not sending.'

### un_events.8
- **Title:** International Court Rules Against Us
- **Description:** The International Court of Justice has issued a ruling against [ROOT.GetCountry.GetName], citing violations of international humanitarian law. The ruling is non-binding but carries enormous symbolic weight. Compliance would require modifications to our military conduct and possible reparations.
- **Flavor:** 'The court has ruled,' the foreign minister said, tossing the document onto the cabinet table. 'We are, it seems, in violation of seventeen articles of international law that half the world's nations have never read.'\n\n'And the other half?' the defence minister asked.\n\n'The other half would prefer we hadn't read them either.'

- **Flavor:** - Earth to Mars in three weeks. Earth to Jupiter in two months. These aren't projections. These are timetables.\n\n- And military applications?\n\n- Any formation, anywhere on Earth, within hours. The concept of distance as a strategic constraint is over.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/antimatter_propulsion_drive.dds

## world_war_events.txt

### world_war_events.1
- **Title:** Ideological Confrontation
- **Description:** [SCOPE.sCountry('ideological_rival').GetName] has issued a series of provocative demands, challenging our ideological stance on the world stage. Their aggressive posture threatens to destabilize the fragile peace between the [Concept('concept_great_power', 'great powers')].
- **Flavor:** The foreign minister read the demands aloud, then set the paper down and removed his spectacles.\n\n'They wish us to renounce our system of government,' he said. 'Publicly. Before the world press.'\n\nThe room was quiet for a long time.\n\n'And if we refuse?'\n\n'Then, I rather think, we shall have our answer about whether they want peace or something else entirely.'
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/ideological_confrontation_speech.dds

### world_war_events.2
- **Title:** Border Incident
- **Description:** A violent skirmish has erupted along the frontier with [SCOPE.sCountry('border_rival').GetName]. Shots were fired and casualties reported. Both sides blame the other. The incident threatens to spiral into something far larger.
- **Flavor:** The lieutenant's hands were still shaking when he filed the report. 'They crossed the line,' he said. 'I gave the order to fire.'\n\n'And the casualties?'\n\n'Three of theirs. One of ours. A corporal, twenty-two years old.'\n\nThe colonel closed the file. Somewhere between this desk and the capital, those numbers would become a crisis.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/border_skirmish_troops.dds

### world_war_events.3
- **Title:** Diplomatic Crisis
- **Description:** [SCOPE.sCountry('crisis_aggressor').GetName] is pressuring smaller nations in our sphere of influence, demanding territorial concessions and political subservience. If we do not act, the balance of power may shift irrevocably.
- **Flavor:** The ambassador from the small nation placed both palms flat on the table, as if to steady himself. 'If your guarantees mean nothing,' he said, 'then say so plainly, and we will make other arrangements.'\n\n'What arrangements?' the foreign minister asked.\n\n'The only kind available to nations without powerful friends: surrender.'
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/diplomatic_crisis_ultimatum.dds

### world_war_events.5
- **Title:** The World at War
- **Description:** The tensions that have been building for years have finally exploded into open conflict. The [Concept('concept_great_power', 'great powers')] have chosen their sides. There is no turning back now - the world is engulfed in the most devastating war in human history.
- **Flavor:** The telegram arrived at three in the morning. The minister read it standing in his dressing gown, his face grey in the lamplight.\n\n'War,' he said. The word hung in the air like smoke.\n\nHis secretary waited, pen in hand. 'Shall I draft the mobilization order?'\n\n'Draft it. Date it. And pray to God that the men who must carry it out are braver than I feel at this moment.'
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/world_war_declaration.dds

### world_war_events.10
- **Title:** Home Front Rally
- **Description:** A surge of patriotic [concept_fervor] sweeps the nation. Citizens line the streets waving flags, factories run double shifts, and volunteers flood recruitment offices. The will to fight has never been stronger.
- **Flavor:** The factory foreman wiped his hands on his apron and addressed the morning shift. 'Double production this week,' he said. 'The front needs shells more than you need sleep.'\n\nNo one complained. The woman at the lathe had received a telegram yesterday. Her husband was not coming home. She picked up her tools and worked a sixteen-hour shift without a word.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/home_front_factory.dds

### world_war_events.11
- **Title:** Strategic Bombing
- **Description:** Enemy bombers have struck our cities, leaving [concept_devastation] in their wake. Fires burn through the night as rescue crews dig through the rubble. The civilian toll mounts, but so does our resolve.
- **Flavor:** The sirens woke the children first. Then the thunder came - not from the sky but from the street, where the grocery had stood that morning.\n\nThe warden found the family in the cellar, covered in plaster dust, the youngest still clutching a wooden horse. 'Everyone accounted for?' he asked.\n\n'Everyone,' the mother said. She did not mention the cat, or the kitchen, or the life they had built above ground. There would be time for that later. Or there would not.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/strategic_bombing_ruins.dds

### world_war_events.12
- **Title:** Resistance Movement
- **Description:** In the occupied territories, a resistance movement has taken root. Brave men and women sabotage enemy supply lines, shelter fugitives, and maintain a flicker of hope in the darkness of occupation.
- **Flavor:** The baker slid the loaves across the counter and, beneath them, a folded note. The customer pocketed it without looking.\n\n'Same time Thursday?' she asked.\n\n'If the flour holds out.'\n\nNeither smiled. In occupied territory, a smile between strangers was as conspicuous as a gunshot.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/resistance_underground.dds

### world_war_events.20
- **Title:** The Hour of Decision
- **Description:** The world war rages on, and we have remained on the sidelines. But the balance of power is shifting, and neutrality grows ever more untenable. [SCOPE.sCountry('ww_main_aggressor').GetName] grows stronger with each passing month. If we do not act soon, the window of opportunity may close forever.
- **Flavor:** The general spread the map across the cabinet table and tapped the front line with a blunt finger. 'Here,' he said. 'And here. If they break through, there will be nothing between them and the coast.'\n\n'And if we intervene?'\n\n'Then we are at war.' He folded his arms. 'But if we do not intervene, excellency, we shall be at their mercy - which, I assure you, is considerably worse.'
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/war_intervention_decision.dds

### world_war_events.30
- **Title:** War Weariness
- **Description:** The war has dragged on far longer than anyone expected. Casualty lists grow longer by the day, food is scarce, and the civilian population is exhausted. Voices demanding peace grow louder - but our enemies show no sign of surrender.
- **Flavor:** The postman no longer knocked. He simply left the telegrams on the step, because the sound of knocking had become something the women on this street could not bear to hear.\n\n'Another one,' the neighbor said, watching from her window. 'The Hendersons.'\n\n'That's their third son.'\n\nSilence. Somewhere, a church bell rang. It had been ringing for so many funerals that no one could remember the last time it rang for joy.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/war_weariness_homefront.dds

### world_war_events.100
- **Title:** The Peace Conference
- **Description:** The guns have fallen silent at last. The victorious powers gather to redraw the map of the world and shape the post-war order. The decisions made here will echo for generations.
- **Flavor:** The delegates filed into the palace hall in silence. Chandeliers blazed overhead; below, the carpet was threadbare from the boots of soldiers quartered there during the siege.\n\n'Shall we begin?' the chairman asked.\n\nA diplomat from the losing side studied his hands. 'We are here to receive your terms,' he said. 'Let us not pretend this is a negotiation.'\n\nThe chairman permitted himself a thin smile. 'Quite right. Shall we call it an opportunity instead?'
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/peace_conference_grand.dds

### world_war_events.101
- **Title:** Regime Change
- **Description:** The victorious powers have demanded a complete transformation of our government. Our former ideology - the one we fought and bled for - is to be dismantled. A new political order will be imposed upon us.
- **Flavor:** The foreign officer placed the document on the desk with the careful courtesy of a man delivering a death sentence. 'Your new constitution,' he said. 'We have taken the liberty of drafting it.'\n\nThe minister stared at the seal - not his nation's seal, but theirs. 'And if we object to its provisions?'\n\n'You misunderstand your position. You may object to the font.'
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/regime_change_occupation.dds

### world_war_events.102
- **Title:** Reconstruction Aid
- **Description:** The victorious powers have offered substantial aid to rebuild our shattered nation. Their generosity comes with strings attached - closer economic ties, political alignment, and a permanent military presence. But the alternative is years of poverty and isolation.
- **Flavor:** The trucks arrived at dawn, stenciled with foreign markings. Canned meat, steel girders, sacks of cement. The mayor stood in the rubble of what had been the town hall and watched them unload.\n\n'Generous of them,' his deputy muttered.\n\n'Generous.' The mayor kicked a piece of masonry. 'Last year they dropped bombs on us. This year, powdered milk. I suppose that is what they call the arc of civilization.'
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/reconstruction_aid_delivery.dds

### world_war_events.103
- **Title:** War Crimes Tribunal
- **Description:** As the fog of war lifts, horrifying revelations emerge about atrocities committed during the conflict. Mass graves, forced labor, systematic brutality - the scale of the crimes shocks the world. The question is: what do we do about it?
- **Flavor:** The prosecutor held up the photograph. The courtroom fell silent.\n\n'The defendant claims he was following orders,' she said. 'Let us examine what those orders produced.'\n\nIn the dock, the old soldier stared straight ahead. He had not spoken since the trial began. His lawyer had advised him to show remorse. He showed nothing at all, and in its way, that was the most damning testimony of the week.
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/war_crimes_tribunal.dds

### world_war_events.104
- **Title:** The Post-War Order
- **Description:** With the great conflict behind us, the victorious powers must decide what kind of world they wish to build. Spheres of influence, new alliances, and international institutions are all on the table.
- **Flavor:** 'We have won the war,' the prime minister said, pouring himself a brandy. 'Now we must win the peace, which, I am given to understand, is considerably more difficult.'\n\n'Spheres of influence?'\n\n'Naturally. The question is how large a sphere our friends will permit us, and how small a sphere we can persuade our enemies to accept.'\n\nHe raised his glass. 'To the new world order. May it last longer than the one we just buried.'
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/post_war_order_map.dds

### world_war_events.105
- **Title:** The New Rivalry
- **Description:** The war is over, but already the seeds of the next conflict are being sown. [SCOPE.sCountry('new_rival_power').GetName] - once our ally of convenience - now stands as the greatest rival to our vision of the world. Two superpowers, two ideologies, one world.
- **Flavor:** The intelligence briefing was three pages long. The analyst summarized it in one sentence: 'They are building what we are building, and they are not building it for friendship.'\n\nThe defence minister closed the folder. 'Six months ago they were our allies.'\n\n'Six months ago we had a common enemy. Now we are each other's.'
- **Current image:** gfx/event_pictures/post_war_order_map.dds
